      <p><b>Latvia</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span> or <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/i/: 'y' in 'happy'">i</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Latvia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/En-us-Latvia.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Latvia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">Latvija</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Latvian" title="Help:IPA/Latvian">[ˈlatvija]</a></span>), officially known as the <b>Republic of Latvia</b> (Latvian: <i lang="lv">Latvijas Republika</i>), is a country in the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_region" title="Baltic region">Baltic region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Since Latvia's independence in 1918, it has been referred to as one of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> to the southeast, and shares a <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime border</a> with <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Latvia has 1,957,200 inhabitants<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> and a territory of 64,589&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (24,938&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_Brief_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_Brief-21">[21]</a></sup> Its capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> other notable <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Latvia#Cities" title="List of cities and towns in Latvia">major cities</a> in Latvia are <a href="/wiki/Daugavpils" title="Daugavpils">Daugavpils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja" title="Liepāja">Liepāja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jelgava" title="Jelgava">Jelgava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valmiera" title="Valmiera">Valmiera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ventspils" title="Ventspils">Ventspils</a> and <a href="/wiki/J%C5%ABrmala" title="Jūrmala">Jūrmala</a>. The country has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">temperate seasonal climate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> The Baltic Sea moderates the climate, although the country has four distinct seasons and snowy winters. </p>
      <p>After centuries of German, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Livonia" title="Swedish Livonia">Swedish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inflanty_Voivodeship" title="Inflanty Voivodeship">Polish-Lithuanian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian rule</a>, a rule mainly executed by the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic German</a> <a href="/wiki/Aristocracy" title="Aristocracy">aristocracy</a>, the Republic of Latvia was established on 18 November 1918 when it broke away from the German empire and declared independence in the aftermath of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Germanis_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Germanis-3">[3]</a></sup> However, by the 1930s the country became increasingly <a href="/wiki/Autocratic" class="mw-redirect" title="Autocratic">autocratic</a> after the <a href="/wiki/1934_Latvian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1934 Latvian coup d'état">coup in 1934</a> establishing an <a href="/wiki/Authoritarian_regime" class="mw-redirect" title="Authoritarian regime">authoritarian regime</a> under <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Ulmanis" title="Kārlis Ulmanis">Kārlis Ulmanis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The country's de facto independence was interrupted at the outset of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, beginning with Latvia's <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_Latvia_in_1940" title="Soviet occupation of Latvia in 1940">forcible incorporation</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, followed by the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Latvia_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Latvia during World War II">invasion and occupation</a> by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in 1941, and the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_re-occupation_of_Latvia_in_1944" title="Soviet re-occupation of Latvia in 1944">re-occupation by the Soviets</a> in 1944 (<a href="/wiki/Courland_Pocket" title="Courland Pocket">Courland Pocket</a> in 1945) to form the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Soviet_Socialist_Republic" title="Latvian Soviet Socialist Republic">Latvian SSR</a> for the next 45 years. </p>
      <p>The peaceful <a href="/wiki/Singing_Revolution" title="Singing Revolution">Singing Revolution</a>, starting in 1987, called for Baltic emancipation from Soviet rule and condemning the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Communist</a> regime's illegal takeover.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> It ended with the <a href="/wiki/On_the_Restoration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia" title="On the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia">Declaration on the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia</a> on 4 May 1990 and restoring de facto <a href="/wiki/State_continuity_of_the_Baltic_states" title="State continuity of the Baltic states">independence</a> on 21 August 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Latvia is a democratic <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_republic" title="Parliamentary republic">parliamentary republic</a>. Capital city Riga served as the <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> in 2014. <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a> is the official language. Latvia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>, divided into 119 <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Latvia" title="Administrative divisions of Latvia">administrative divisions</a>, of which 110 are municipalities and nine are cities.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Latvians" title="Latvians">Latvians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Livonians" title="Livonians">Livonians</a> are the indigenous people of Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_Brief_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_Brief-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a> are the only two surviving <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">Baltic languages</a>. </p>
      <p>Despite foreign rule from the 13th to 20th centuries, the Latvian nation maintained its identity throughout the generations via the language and musical traditions. However, as a consequence of centuries of Russian rule (1710–1918) and later <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_the_Baltic_states" title="Occupation of the Baltic states">Soviet occupation</a>, 26.9% of the population of Latvia are <a href="/wiki/Russians_in_Latvia" title="Russians in Latvia">ethnic Russians</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mfa.gov.lv_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mfa.gov.lv-28">[28]</a></sup> some of whom (10.7% of Latvian residents<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>) have not gained citizenship, leaving them with <a href="/wiki/Non-citizens_(Latvia)" title="Non-citizens (Latvia)">no citizenship</a> at all. Until World War II, Latvia also had significant minorities of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Germans</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latvia" title="History of the Jews in Latvia">Jews</a>. Latvia is historically predominantly <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>, except for the <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">Latgale</a> region in the southeast, which has historically been predominantly <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> The Russian population is largely <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a> Christians. </p>
      <p>Latvia is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a> with an advanced, <a href="/wiki/High-income_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="High-income economy">high-income economy</a> <sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> and ranks 39th in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> It performs favorably in measurements of <a href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World_(report)" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedom in the World (report)">civil liberties</a>, <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">press freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_and_surveillance_by_country" title="Internet censorship and surveillance by country">internet freedom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">democratic governance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">living standards</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">peacefulness</a>. Latvia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_of_the_Baltic_Sea_States" title="Council of the Baltic Sea States">CBSS</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">IMF</a>, <a href="/wiki/NB8" class="mw-redirect" title="NB8">NB8</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordic_Investment_Bank" title="Nordic Investment Bank">NIB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">OSCE</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">WTO</a>. A full member of the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>, it began using the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as its currency on 1 January 2014, replacing the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_lats" title="Latvian lats">Latvian lats</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
