      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Latvia" title="Geography of Latvia">Geography of Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Europe" title="Northern Europe">Northern Europe</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kolkas_rags.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kolkas_rags.jpg/220px-Kolkas_rags.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kolkas_rags.jpg/330px-Kolkas_rags.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Kolkas_rags.jpg/440px-Kolkas_rags.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kolkas_rags.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Cape_Kolka" title="Cape Kolka">Cape Kolka</a>, the northern tip of Latvia in the Gulf of Riga
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png/220px-BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="305" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png/330px-BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png/440px-BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png 2x" data-file-width="1118" data-file-height="1548"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:BalticSea_March2000_NASA-S2000084115409.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Latvia lies in Northern Europe, on the eastern shores of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Latvia lies in Northern Europe, on the eastern shores of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> and northwestern part of the <a href="/wiki/East_European_craton" class="mw-redirect" title="East European craton">East European Craton</a> (EEC), between latitudes <a href="/wiki/55th_parallel_north" title="55th parallel north">55°</a> and <a href="/wiki/58th_parallel_north" title="58th parallel north">58° N</a> (a small area is north of 58°), and longitudes <a href="/wiki/21st_meridian_east" title="21st meridian east">21°</a> and <a href="/wiki/29th_meridian_east" title="29th meridian east">29° E</a> (a small area is west of 21°). Latvia has a total area of 64,559&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (24,926&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of which 62,157&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (23,999&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) land, 18,159&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (7,011&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) agricultural land,<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_–_Key_Indicators_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_–_Key_Indicators-92">[92]</a></sup> 34,964&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (13,500&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) forest land<sup id="cite_ref-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators-93">[93]</a></sup> and 2,402&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (927&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) inland water.<sup id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The total length of Latvia's boundary is 1,866&nbsp;km (1,159&nbsp;mi). The total length of its land boundary is 1,368&nbsp;km (850&nbsp;mi), of which 343&nbsp;km (213&nbsp;mi) is shared with <a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> to the north, 276&nbsp;km (171&nbsp;mi) with the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Federation">Russian Federation</a> to the east, 161&nbsp;km (100&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> to the southeast and 588&nbsp;km (365&nbsp;mi) with <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> to the south. The total length of its <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime boundary</a> is 498&nbsp;km (309&nbsp;mi), which is shared with Estonia, <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>. Extension from north to south is 210&nbsp;km (130&nbsp;mi) and from west to east 450&nbsp;km (280&nbsp;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Most of Latvia's territory is less than 100&nbsp;m (330&nbsp;ft) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>. Its largest lake, <a href="/wiki/Lub%C4%81ns" class="mw-redirect" title="Lubāns">Lubāns</a>, has an area of 80.7&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (31.2&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi), its deepest lake, <a href="/wiki/Dr%C4%ABdzis" class="mw-redirect" title="Drīdzis">Drīdzis</a>, is 65.1&nbsp;m (214&nbsp;ft) deep. The longest river on Latvian territory is the <a href="/wiki/Gauja" title="Gauja">Gauja</a>, at 452&nbsp;km (281&nbsp;mi) in length. The longest river flowing through Latvian territory is the <a href="/wiki/Daugava_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava River">Daugava</a>, which has a total length of 1,005&nbsp;km (624&nbsp;mi), of which 352&nbsp;km (219&nbsp;mi) is on Latvian territory. Latvia's highest point is <a href="/wiki/Gaizi%C5%86kalns" title="Gaiziņkalns">Gaiziņkalns</a>, 311.6&nbsp;m (1,022&nbsp;ft). The length of Latvia's <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic</a> coastline is 494&nbsp;km (307&nbsp;mi). An inlet of the Baltic Sea, the shallow <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Riga" title="Gulf of Riga">Gulf of Riga</a> is situated in the northwest of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_brief_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_brief-95">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/220px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/330px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png/440px-Koppen_World_Map_Dfb_Dwb_Dsb.png 2x" data-file-width="4231" data-file-height="2592"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style>
           <div class="legend">
            <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#38C7FF; color:black;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Humid continental climate warm summer subtype
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/220px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/330px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png/440px-Koppen_classification_worldmap_CfbCfc.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1280"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959">
           <div class="legend">
            <span class="legend-color" style="background-color:#008000; color:white;">&nbsp;</span>&nbsp;Oceanic climate
           </div>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Latvia has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate" class="mw-redirect" title="Temperate">temperate</a> climate that has been described in various sources as either <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental" class="mw-redirect" title="Humid continental">humid continental</a> (<a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate#Dfb/Dwb/Dsb:_Warm_summer_subtype" title="Humid continental climate">Köppen <i>Dfb</i></a>) or <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic/maritime</a> (Köppen <i>Cfb</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-liepu_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liepu-96">[96]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Coastal regions, especially the western coast of the <a href="/wiki/Courland_Peninsula" title="Courland Peninsula">Courland Peninsula</a>, possess a more maritime climate with cooler summers and milder winters, while eastern parts exhibit a more continental climate with warmer summers and harsher winters.<sup id="cite_ref-liepu_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-liepu-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvia has four pronounced seasons of near-equal length. Winter starts in mid-December and lasts until mid-March. Winters have average temperatures of −6&nbsp;°C (21&nbsp;°F) and are characterized by stable snow cover, bright sunshine, and short days. Severe spells of winter weather with cold winds, extreme temperatures of around −30&nbsp;°C (−22&nbsp;°F) and heavy snowfalls are common. Summer starts in June and lasts until August. Summers are usually warm and sunny, with cool evenings and nights. Summers have average temperatures of around 19&nbsp;°C (66&nbsp;°F), with extremes of 35&nbsp;°C (95&nbsp;°F). Spring and autumn bring fairly mild weather.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>

      <p>2019 was the warmest year in the history of weather observation in Latvia with an average temperature +8.1°C higher.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/220px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/330px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG/440px-Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Turaidas_skats_uz_Gauju_2okt04.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Latvia has the fifth highest proportion of land covered by forests in the European Union.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most of the country is composed of fertile lowland plains and moderate hills. In a typical Latvian landscape, a mosaic of vast forests alternates with fields, farmsteads, and pastures. Arable land is spotted with birch groves and wooded clusters, which afford a habitat for numerous plants and animals. Latvia has hundreds of kilometres of undeveloped seashore—lined by pine forests, dunes, and continuous white sand beaches.<sup id="cite_ref-Latvia_in_brief_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Latvia_in_brief-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvia has the 5th highest proportion of land covered by forests in the European Union, after Sweden, Finland, Estonia and Slovenia.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Forests account for 3,497,000&nbsp;ha (8,640,000 acres) or 56% of the total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators-93">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvia has over 12,500 rivers, which stretch for 38,000&nbsp;km (24,000&nbsp;mi). Major rivers include the <a href="/wiki/Daugava_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Daugava River">Daugava River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lielupe" title="Lielupe">Lielupe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gauja" title="Gauja">Gauja</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venta" title="Venta">Venta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Salaca" title="Salaca">Salaca</a>, the largest spawning ground for <a href="/wiki/Salmon" title="Salmon">salmon</a> in the eastern Baltic states. There are 2,256 lakes that are bigger than 1&nbsp;ha (2.5 acres), with a collective area of 1,000&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (390&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). <a href="/wiki/Mire" title="Mire">Mires</a> occupy 9.9% of Latvia's territory. Of these, 42% are raised bogs; 49% are fens; and 9% are transitional mires. 70% percent of the mires are untouched by civilization, and they are a refuge for many rare species of plants and animals.<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agricultural areas account for 1,815,900&nbsp;ha (4,487,000 acres) or 29% of the total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-Agriculture_–_Key_Indicators_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Agriculture_–_Key_Indicators-92">[92]</a></sup> With the dismantling of collective farms, the area devoted to farming decreased dramatically – now farms are predominantly small. Approximately 200 farms, occupying 2,750&nbsp;ha (6,800 acres), are engaged in ecologically pure farming (using no artificial fertilizers or pesticides).<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvia's <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national parks</a> are <a href="/wiki/Gauja_National_Park" title="Gauja National Park">Gauja National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">Vidzeme</a> (since 1973),<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C4%B6emeri_National_Park" title="Ķemeri National Park">Ķemeri National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Zemgale" class="mw-redirect" title="Zemgale">Zemgale</a> (1997), <a href="/wiki/Sl%C4%ABtere_National_Park" title="Slītere National Park">Slītere National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">Kurzeme</a> (1999), and <a href="/wiki/R%C4%81zna_National_Park" title="Rāzna National Park">Rāzna National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">Latgale</a> (2007).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvia has a long tradition of conservation. The first laws and regulations were promulgated in the 16th and 17th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> There are 706 specially state-level protected natural areas in Latvia: four national parks, one biosphere reserve, 42 nature parks, nine areas of protected landscapes, 260 nature reserves, four strict nature reserves, 355 nature monuments, seven protected marine areas and 24 microreserves.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Nationally protected areas account for 12,790&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (4,940&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) or around 20% of Latvia's total land area.<sup id="cite_ref-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geographical_Data_–_Key_Indicators-94">[94]</a></sup> Latvia's Red Book (Endangered Species List of Latvia), which was established in 1977, contains 112 plant species and 119 animal species. Latvia has ratified the international Washington, Bern, and Ramsare conventions.<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2012 <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> ranks Latvia second, after <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, based on the environmental performance of the country's policies.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Latvia is much higher than world average. In 2016, Latvia had 8.5 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-108">[108]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much more than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> In 2016 Latvia used 6.4 global hectares of biocapacity per person - their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use less biocapacity than Latvia contains. As a result, Latvia is running a biocapacity reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-108">[108]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:White-Wagtail.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/220px-White-Wagtail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/330px-White-Wagtail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/White-Wagtail.jpg/440px-White-Wagtail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="732" data-file-height="571"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:White-Wagtail.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/White_wagtail" title="White wagtail">white wagtail</a> is the national bird of Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Approximately 30,000 species of flora and fauna have been registered in Latvia.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Common species of wildlife in Latvia include <a href="/wiki/Roe_deer" title="Roe deer">deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">wild boar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">lynx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brown_bear" title="Brown bear">bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurasian_beaver" title="Eurasian beaver">beaver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray wolf">wolves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_non-marine_molluscs_of_Latvia" title="List of non-marine molluscs of Latvia">Non-marine molluscs of Latvia</a> include 159 species.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Species that are endangered in other European countries but common in Latvia include: black stork (<i><a href="/wiki/Ciconia_nigra" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciconia nigra">Ciconia nigra</a></i>), corncrake (<i><a href="/wiki/Crex_crex" class="mw-redirect" title="Crex crex">Crex crex</a></i>), lesser spotted eagle (<i><a href="/wiki/Aquila_pomarina" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquila pomarina">Aquila pomarina</a></i>), white-backed woodpecker (<i><a href="/wiki/Picoides_leucotos" class="mw-redirect" title="Picoides leucotos">Picoides leucotos</a></i>), Eurasian crane (<i><a href="/wiki/Grus_grus" class="mw-redirect" title="Grus grus">Grus grus</a></i>), Eurasian beaver (<i><a href="/wiki/Castor_fiber" class="mw-redirect" title="Castor fiber">Castor fiber</a></i>), Eurasian otter (<i><a href="/wiki/Lutra_lutra" class="mw-redirect" title="Lutra lutra">Lutra lutra</a></i>), European wolf (<i><a href="/wiki/Canis_lupus" class="mw-redirect" title="Canis lupus">Canis lupus</a></i>) and European lynx (<i><a href="/wiki/Eurasian_lynx" title="Eurasian lynx">Felis lynx</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia_102-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nature_and_Environment_in_Latvia-102">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Latvia is shared between the Central European and Northern European provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Latvia belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sarmatic_mixed_forests" title="Sarmatic mixed forests">Sarmatic mixed forests</a>. 56 percent<sup id="cite_ref-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Forestry_–_Key_Indicators-93">[93]</a></sup> of Latvia's territory is covered by forests, mostly <a href="/wiki/Scots_pine" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots pine">Scots pine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birch" title="Birch">birch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norway_spruce" class="mw-redirect" title="Norway spruce">Norway spruce</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 2.09/10, ranking it 159<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-113">[113]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several species of flora and fauna are considered national symbols. <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">Oak</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Quercus_robur" title="Quercus robur">Quercus robur</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">ozols</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Tilia" title="Tilia">linden</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Tilia_cordata" title="Tilia cordata">Tilia cordata</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">liepa</i>) are Latvia's national trees and the <a href="/wiki/Leucanthemum_vulgare" title="Leucanthemum vulgare">daisy</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Leucanthemum_vulgare" title="Leucanthemum vulgare">Leucanthemum vulgare</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">pīpene</i>) its national flower. The white wagtail (<i><a href="/wiki/White_wagtail" title="White wagtail">Motacilla alba</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">baltā cielava</i>) is Latvia's national bird. Its national insect is the <a href="/wiki/Adalia_bipunctata" title="Adalia bipunctata">two-spot ladybird</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Adalia_bipunctata" title="Adalia bipunctata">Adalia bipunctata</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">divpunktu mārīte</i>). <a href="/wiki/Amber" title="Amber">Amber</a>, fossilized tree resin, is one of Latvia's most important cultural symbols. In ancient times, amber found along the Baltic Sea coast was sought by Vikings as well as traders from Egypt, Greece and the Roman Empire. This led to the development of the <a href="/wiki/Amber_Road" title="Amber Road">Amber Road</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Several nature reserves protect unspoiled landscapes with a variety of large animals. At <a href="/wiki/Pape_Nature_Reserve" title="Pape Nature Reserve">Pape Nature Reserve</a>, where <a href="/wiki/European_bison" title="European bison">European bison</a>, wild horses, and <a href="/wiki/Heck_cattle" title="Heck cattle">recreated aurochs</a> have been reintroduced, there is now an almost complete <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a> <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafauna</a> also including moose, deer, and wolf.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Latvija_viki.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/360px-Latvija_viki.PNG" decoding="async" width="360" height="223" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/540px-Latvija_viki.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Latvija_viki.PNG/720px-Latvija_viki.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1001" data-file-height="620"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Latvija_viki.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Historical regions: orange <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">Courland</a>, green <a href="/wiki/Semigallia" title="Semigallia">Semigallia</a>, yellow <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">Vidzeme</a>, blue <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">Latgale</a>, brown <a href="/wiki/Selonia" title="Selonia">Selonia</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_novadi_(kr%C4%81s%C4%81s).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/360px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png" decoding="async" width="360" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/540px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png/720px-Latvijas_novadi_%28kr%C4%81s%C4%81s%29.png 2x" data-file-width="2536" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_novadi_(kr%C4%81s%C4%81s).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Administrative divisions of Latvia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Latvia" title="Administrative divisions of Latvia">Administrative divisions of Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Latvia">List of cities in Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Planning_regions_of_Latvia" title="Planning regions of Latvia">Planning regions of Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Statistical_regions_of_Latvia" title="Statistical regions of Latvia">Statistical regions of Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Historical_regions_of_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Historical regions of Latvia">Historical regions of Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Latvia is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary state</a>, currently divided into 110 one-level municipalities (<a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">novadi</i>) and 9 republican cities (<a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">republikas pilsētas</i>) with their own city council and administration: <a href="/wiki/Daugavpils" title="Daugavpils">Daugavpils</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C4%93kabpils" title="Jēkabpils">Jēkabpils</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jelgava" title="Jelgava">Jelgava</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C5%ABrmala" title="Jūrmala">Jūrmala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liep%C4%81ja" title="Liepāja">Liepāja</a>, <a href="/wiki/R%C4%93zekne" title="Rēzekne">Rēzekne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valmiera" title="Valmiera">Valmiera</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ventspils" title="Ventspils">Ventspils</a>. There are four <a href="/wiki/Cultural_regions_of_Latvia" title="Cultural regions of Latvia">historical and cultural regions in Latvia</a>&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Courland" title="Courland">Courland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latgale" title="Latgale">Latgale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vidzeme" title="Vidzeme">Vidzeme</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zemgale" class="mw-redirect" title="Zemgale">Zemgale</a>, which are recognised in <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Latvia" title="Constitution of Latvia">Constitution of Latvia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Selonia" title="Selonia">Selonia</a>, a part of Zemgale, is sometimes considered culturally distinct region, but it is not part of any formal division. The borders of historical and cultural regions usually are not explicitly defined and in several sources may vary. In formal divisions, Riga region, which includes the capital and parts of other regions that have a strong relationship with the capital, is also often included in regional divisions; e.g., there are five <a href="/wiki/Planning_regions_of_Latvia" title="Planning regions of Latvia">planning regions of Latvia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a>: <i lang="lv">plānošanas reģioni</i>), which were created in 2009 to promote balanced development of all regions. Under this division Riga region includes large parts of what traditionally is considered Vidzeme, Courland, and Zemgale. <a href="/wiki/Statistical_regions_of_Latvia" title="Statistical regions of Latvia">Statistical regions of Latvia</a>, established in accordance with the EU <a href="/wiki/Nomenclature_of_Territorial_Units_for_Statistics" title="Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics">Nomenclature of Territorial Units for Statistics</a>, duplicate this division, but divides Riga region into two parts with the capital alone being a separate region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The largest city in Latvia is Riga, the second largest city is Daugavpils and the third largest city is Liepaja. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Latvia" title="Politics of Latvia">Politics of Latvia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliament of Latvia">Parliament of Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Latvia" title="Government of Latvia">Government of Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:left; float:left; margin-right:9px; margin-left:2px;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/File:Egils_Levits.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Egils Levits.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Egils_Levits.jpg/125px-Egils_Levits.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="187" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Egils_Levits.jpg/188px-Egils_Levits.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Egils_Levits.jpg/250px-Egils_Levits.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1339" data-file-height="2008"></a> </td>

        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Egils_Levits" title="Egils Levits">Egils Levits</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/President_of_Latvia" title="President of Latvia">President</a></small> </td> 
         <td style="text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/Arturs_Kri%C5%A1j%C4%81nis_Kari%C5%86%C5%A1" title="Arturs Krišjānis Kariņš">Arturs Krišjānis Kariņš</a><br><small><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Latvia" title="Prime Minister of Latvia">Prime Minister</a></small> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The 100-seat <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> Latvian parliament, the <i><a href="/wiki/Saeima" title="Saeima">Saeima</a></i>, is <a href="/wiki/General_election" title="General election">elected</a> by direct popular vote every four years. The president is elected by the <i>Saeima</i> in a separate election, also held every four years. The president appoints a prime minister who, together with his cabinet, forms the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive branch</a> of the government, which has to receive a confidence vote by the <i>Saeima</i>. This system also existed before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-116">[116]</a></sup> The most senior civil servants are the thirteen <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of State">Secretaries of State</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_(6).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/220px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/330px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg/440px-Flickr_-_Saeima_-_4.maijs_Saeim%C4%81_%286%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000"></a>
