       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The largest religion in Latvia is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (79%).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_174-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup> The largest groups as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> were: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_of_Latvia" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church of Latvia">Evangelical Lutheran Church of Latvia</a>&nbsp;– 708,773<sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Latvia">Roman Catholic</a>&nbsp;– 500,000<sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox</a>&nbsp;– 370,000<sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Riga_Dom_02.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Riga_Dom_02.JPG/220px-Riga_Dom_02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Riga_Dom_02.JPG/330px-Riga_Dom_02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Riga_Dom_02.JPG/440px-Riga_Dom_02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4592" data-file-height="3312"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Riga_Dom_02.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Riga_Cathedral" title="Riga Cathedral">Riga Cathedral</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> Poll 2010, 38% of Latvian citizens responded that "they believe there is a God", while 48% answered that "they believe there is some sort of spirit or life force" and 11% stated that "they do not believe there is any sort of spirit, God, or life force". </p>
      <p>Lutheranism was more prominent before the Soviet occupation, when it was a majority religion of ~60% due to strong historical links with the <a href="/wiki/Nordic_countries" title="Nordic countries">Nordic countries</a> and to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Hanseatic_League" title="Hanseatic League">Hansa</a> in particular and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> in general. Since then, Lutheranism has declined to a slightly greater extent than Roman Catholicism in all three <a href="/wiki/Baltic_states" title="Baltic states">Baltic states</a>. The Evangelical Lutheran Church, with an estimated 600,000 members in 1956, was affected most adversely. An internal document of 18 March 1987, near the end of communist rule, spoke of an active membership that had shrunk to only 25,000 in Latvia, but the faith has since experienced a revival.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country's Orthodox Christians belong to the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Orthodox_Church" title="Latvian Orthodox Church">Latvian Orthodox Church</a>, a semi-autonomous body within the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>. In 2011, there were 416 religious <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latvia" title="History of the Jews in Latvia">Jews</a>, 319 <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Latvia" title="Islam in Latvia">Muslims</a> and 102 <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Hinduism in Latvia">Hindus</a>. Most of the Hindus are local converts from the work of the <a href="/wiki/Hare_Krishna_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Hare Krishna movement">Hare Krishna movement</a>; some are foreign workers from India.<sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup> As of 2004 there were more than 600 Latvian <a href="/wiki/Neopaganism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neopaganism">neopagans</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Dievtur%C4%ABba" title="Dievturība">Dievturi</a></i> (The Godskeepers), whose religion is based on <a href="/wiki/Latvian_mythology" title="Latvian mythology">Latvian mythology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> About 21% of the total population is not affiliated with a specific religion.<sup id="cite_ref-Tieslietu_Ministrija_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tieslietu_Ministrija-2">[2]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education_and_science">Education and science</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Education and science">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Latvia" title="Education in Latvia">Education in Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="List of universities in Latvia">List of universities in Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg/280px-Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg/420px-Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg/560px-Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10240" data-file-height="4846"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Latvijas_Universit%C4%81te_-_ogre11_-_Panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/University_of_Latvia" title="University of Latvia">University of Latvia</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Latvia" title="University of Latvia">University of Latvia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Riga_Technical_University" title="Riga Technical University">Riga Technical University</a> are two major universities in the country, both established on the basis of<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="please clarify the relationships among these institutions throughout (what does &quot;established on the base of&quot; or &quot;established on the basis of&quot; mean?) (September 2019)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Riga Polytechnical Institute and located in <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> Other important universities, which were established on the base of State University of Latvia, include the <a href="/wiki/Latvia_University_of_Life_Sciences_and_Technologies" title="Latvia University of Life Sciences and Technologies">Latvia University of Life Sciences and Technologies</a> (established in 1939 on the basis of the Faculty of Agriculture) and <a href="/wiki/Riga_Stradi%C5%86%C5%A1_University" title="Riga Stradiņš University">Riga Stradiņš University</a> (established in 1950 on the basis of the Faculty of Medicine). Both nowadays cover a variety of different fields. The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Daugavpils" title="University of Daugavpils">University of Daugavpils</a> is another significant centre of education. </p>
      <p>Latvia closed 131 schools between 2006 and 2010, which is a 12.9% decline, and in the same period enrolment in educational institutions has fallen by over 54,000 people, a 10.3% decline.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Latvian policy in science and technology has set out the long-term goal of transitioning from labor-consuming economy to knowledge-based economy.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> By 2020 the government aims to spend 1.5% of GDP on research and development, with half of the investments coming from the private sector. Latvia plans to base the development of its scientific potential on existing scientific traditions, particularly in organic chemistry, medical chemistry, genetic engineering, physics, materials science and information technologies.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup> The greatest number of patents, both nationwide and abroad, are in medical chemistry.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Latvia" title="Health in Latvia">Health in Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Latvian healthcare system is a <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal programme</a>, largely funded through government taxation.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> It is among the lowest-ranked healthcare systems in Europe, due to excessive waiting times for treatment, insufficient access to the latest medicines, and other factors.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> There were 59 hospitals in Latvia in 2009, down from 94 in 2007 and 121 in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-211">[211]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Latvia" title="Culture of Latvia">Culture of Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Traditional Latvian <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a>, especially the dance of the <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk songs</a>, dates back well over a thousand years. More than 1.2 million texts and 30,000 melodies of folk songs have been identified.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Between the 13th and 19th centuries, <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Germans" title="Baltic Germans">Baltic Germans</a>, many of whom were originally of non-German ancestry but had been assimilated into <a href="/wiki/German_language_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="German language in Europe">German culture</a>, formed the upper class.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> They developed distinct cultural heritage, characterised by both Latvian and German influences. It has survived in German Baltic families to this day, in spite of their dispersal to Germany, the United States, Canada and other countries in the early 20th century. However, most indigenous Latvians did not participate in this particular cultural life.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Thus, the mostly peasant local <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> heritage was preserved, partly merging with Christian traditions. For example, one of the most popular celebrations is <a href="/wiki/J%C4%81%C5%86i" title="Jāņi">Jāņi</a>, a pagan celebration of the <a href="/wiki/Summer_solstice" title="Summer solstice">summer solstice</a>—which Latvians celebrate on the feast day of St. <a href="/wiki/John_the_Baptist" title="John the Baptist">John the Baptist</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg/220px-Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg/330px-Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg/440px-Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Centre_of_Riga-112610.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Historic_Centre_of_Riga" class="mw-redirect" title="Historic Centre of Riga">Historic Centre of Riga</a> was declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1997.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the 19th century, Latvian nationalist movements emerged. They promoted Latvian culture and encouraged Latvians to take part in cultural activities. The 19th century and beginning of the 20th century is often regarded by Latvians as a classical era of Latvian culture. Posters show the influence of other European cultures, for example, works of artists such as the Baltic-German artist <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Borchert" title="Bernhard Borchert">Bernhard Borchert</a> and the French <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Dufy" title="Raoul Dufy">Raoul Dufy</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> With the onset of World War II, many Latvian artists and other members of the cultural elite fled the country yet continued to produce their work, largely for a Latvian émigré audience.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Song_and_Dance_Festival" title="Latvian Song and Dance Festival">Latvian Song and Dance Festival</a> is an important event in <a href="/wiki/Latvians" title="Latvians">Latvian</a> culture and social life. It has been held since 1873, normally every five years. Approximately 30,000 performers altogether participate in the event.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup> Folk songs and classical choir songs are sung, with emphasis on <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> singing, though modern popular songs have recently been incorporated into the repertoire as well.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After incorporation into the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, Latvian artists and writers were forced to follow the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">socialist realism</a> style of art. During the Soviet era, music became increasingly popular, with the most popular being songs from the 1980s. At this time, songs often made fun of the characteristics of Soviet life and were concerned about preserving Latvian identity. This aroused popular protests against the USSR and also gave rise to an increasing popularity of poetry. Since independence, theatre, <a href="/wiki/Scenography" title="Scenography">scenography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Choir" title="Choir">choir</a> music, and classical music have become the most notable branches of Latvian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During July 2014, <a href="/wiki/Riga" title="Riga">Riga</a> hosted the 8th <a href="/wiki/World_Choir_Games" title="World Choir Games">World Choir Games</a> as it played host to over 27,000 choristers representing over 450 choirs and over 70 countries. The festival is the biggest of its kind in the world and is held every two years in a different host city.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[219]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Starting in 2019 Latvia hosts the inaugural <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://riga-jurmala.com/">Riga Jurmala Music Festival</a>, a new festival in which world-famous orchestras and conductors perform across four weekends during the summer. The festival takes place at the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_National_Opera" title="Latvian National Opera">Latvian National Opera</a>, the Great Guild, and the Great and Small Halls of the Dzintari Concert Hall. This year features the <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Radio_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Bavarian Radio Symphony Orchestra">Bavarian Radio Symphony Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Israel_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Israel Philharmonic Orchestra">Israel Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, the <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> and the Russian National Orchestra.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Latvian_cuisine" title="Latvian cuisine">Latvian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Latvian cuisine typically consists of agricultural products, with meat featuring in most main meal dishes. Fish is commonly consumed due to Latvia's location on the Baltic Sea. Latvian cuisine has been influenced by the neighbouring countries. Common ingredients in Latvian recipes are found locally, such as potatoes, wheat, barley, cabbage, onions, eggs, and pork. Latvian food is generally quite fatty, and uses few spices.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Grey peas and ham are generally considered as staple foods of Latvians. <a href="/wiki/Sorrel_soup" title="Sorrel soup">Sorrel soup</a> (<i>skābeņu zupa</i>) is also consumed by Latvians.<sup id="cite_ref-latvianfood_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latvianfood-222">[222]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rupjmaize" title="Rupjmaize">Rupjmaize</a> is a dark bread made from rye, considered the national <a href="/wiki/Staple_food" title="Staple food">staple</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Latvia" title="Sport in Latvia">Sport in Latvia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG/220px-Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG/330px-Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG/440px-Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2095" data-file-height="1501"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Arena_Riga_CAN-CZE-2006-05-14.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Arena_Riga" class="mw-redirect" title="Arena Riga">Arena Riga</a> during the <a href="/wiki/2006_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2006 IIHF World Championship">2006 IIHF World Championship</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Ice hockey is usually considered the most popular sport in Latvia. Latvia has had many famous hockey stars like <a href="/wiki/Helmuts_Balderis" title="Helmuts Balderis">Helmuts Balderis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art%C5%ABrs_Irbe" title="Artūrs Irbe">Artūrs Irbe</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C4%81rlis_Skrasti%C5%86%C5%A1" title="Kārlis Skrastiņš">Kārlis Skrastiņš</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandis_Ozoli%C5%86%C5%A1" title="Sandis Ozoliņš">Sandis Ozoliņš</a> and more recently <a href="/wiki/Zemgus_Girgensons" title="Zemgus Girgensons">Zemgus Girgensons</a>, whom the Latvian people have strongly supported in international and NHL play, expressed through the dedication of using the NHL's All Star Voting to bring Zemgus to number one in voting.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dinamo_Riga" title="Dinamo Riga">Dinamo Riga</a> is the country's strongest hockey club, playing in the <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">Kontinental Hockey League</a>. The national tournament is the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_Hockey_Higher_League" title="Latvian Hockey Higher League">Latvian Hockey Higher League</a>, held since 1931. The <a href="/wiki/2006_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2006 IIHF World Championship">2006 IIHF World Championship</a> was held in Riga. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg/150px-Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="242" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg/225px-Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg/300px-Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1331" data-file-height="2151"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kristaps_Porzingis.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Kristaps_Porzi%C5%86%C4%A3is" title="Kristaps Porziņģis">Kristaps Porziņģis</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The second most popular sport is basketball. Latvia has a long basketball tradition, as the <a href="/wiki/Latvian_national_basketball_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian national basketball team">Latvian national basketball team</a> won the first ever <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket" title="EuroBasket">EuroBasket</a> in <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_1935" title="EuroBasket 1935">1935</a> and silver medals in <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_1939" title="EuroBasket 1939">1939</a>, after losing the final to <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="Lithuania men's national basketball team">Lithuania</a> by one point. Latvia has had many European basketball stars like <a href="/wiki/J%C4%81nis_Kr%C5%ABmi%C5%86%C5%A1" title="Jānis Krūmiņš">Jānis Krūmiņš</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maigonis_Valdmanis" title="Maigonis Valdmanis">Maigonis Valdmanis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valdis_Mui%C5%BEnieks" title="Valdis Muižnieks">Valdis Muižnieks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valdis_Valters" title="Valdis Valters">Valdis Valters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Igors_Miglinieks" title="Igors Miglinieks">Igors Miglinieks</a>, as well as the first Latvian <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> player <a href="/wiki/Gundars_V%C4%93tra" title="Gundars Vētra">Gundars Vētra</a>. <a href="/wiki/Andris_Biedri%C5%86%C5%A1" title="Andris Biedriņš">Andris Biedriņš</a> is one of the most well-known Latvian basketball players, who played in the <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_State_Warriors" title="Golden State Warriors">Golden State Warriors</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Jazz" title="Utah Jazz">Utah Jazz</a>. Current <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> players include <a href="/wiki/Kristaps_Porzi%C5%86%C4%A3is" title="Kristaps Porziņģis">Kristaps Porziņģis</a>, who plays for the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a>, <a href="/wiki/D%C4%81vis_Bert%C4%81ns" title="Dāvis Bertāns">Dāvis Bertāns</a>, who plays for the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Wizards" title="Washington Wizards">Washington Wizards</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rodions_Kurucs" title="Rodions Kurucs">Rodions Kurucs</a>, who plays for the <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn_Nets" title="Brooklyn Nets">Brooklyn Nets</a>. Former Latvian basketball club <a href="/wiki/R%C4%ABgas_ASK" title="Rīgas ASK">Rīgas ASK</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Euroleague_Basketball" title="Euroleague Basketball">Euroleague</a> tournament three times in a row before becoming defunct. Currently, <a href="/wiki/BK_VEF_R%C4%ABga" title="BK VEF Rīga">VEF Rīga</a>, which competes in <a href="/wiki/Eurocup_Basketball" class="mw-redirect" title="Eurocup Basketball">EuroCup</a>, is the strongest professional basketball club in Latvia. <a href="/wiki/BK_Ventspils" title="BK Ventspils">BK Ventspils</a>, which participates in <a href="/wiki/EuroChallenge" class="mw-redirect" title="EuroChallenge">EuroChallenge</a>, is the second strongest basketball club in Latvia, previously winning <a href="/wiki/Latvijas_Basketbola_l%C4%ABga" title="Latvijas Basketbola līga">LBL</a> eight times and <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Basketball_League" title="Baltic Basketball League">BBL</a> in 2013.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Latvia was one of the <a href="/wiki/EuroBasket_2015" title="EuroBasket 2015">EuroBasket 2015</a> hosts. </p>
      <p>Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Floorball" title="Floorball">floorball</a>, tennis, volleyball, cycling, <a href="/wiki/Bobsleigh" title="Bobsleigh">bobsleigh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skeleton_(sport)" title="Skeleton (sport)">skeleton</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Latvian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Latvian national football team">Latvian national football team</a>'s only major <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> tournament participation has been the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">2004 UEFA European Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uefa.com_2015-11-03_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uefa.com_2015-11-03-226">[226]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Latvia_at_the_Olympics" title="Latvia at the Olympics">Latvia</a> has participated successfully in both <a href="/wiki/Winter_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Winter Olympics">Winter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a>. The most successful Olympic athlete in the history of independent Latvia has been <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ris_%C5%A0trombergs" title="Māris Štrombergs">Māris Štrombergs</a>, who became a two-time Olympic champion in 2008 and 2012 at Men's BMX.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Boxing, <a href="/wiki/Mairis_Briedis" title="Mairis Briedis">Mairis Briedis</a> is the first Latvian to win a boxing world title, having held the WBC cruiserweight title from 2017 to 2018, and the WBO cruiserweight title in 2019. </p>
      <p>In 2017, Latvian tennis player <a href="/wiki/Je%C4%BCena_Ostapenko" title="Jeļena Ostapenko">Jeļena Ostapenko</a> won the <a href="/wiki/2017_French_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_Singles" title="2017 French Open – Women's Singles">2017 French Open Women's singles title</a> being the first unseeded player to do so in the open era. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Latvia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>

         <li id="cite_note-26"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-26">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On 21 August 1991, after the <a href="/wiki/1991_Soviet_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="1991 Soviet coup d'état attempt">Soviet coup d'état attempt</a>, the Supreme Council adopted a Constitutional law, "<a href="/wiki/On_the_Restoration_of_Independence_of_the_Republic_of_Latvia#Further_developments" title="On the Restoration of Independence of the Republic of Latvia">On statehood of the Republic of Latvia</a>", declaring Article 5 of the Declaration to be invalid, thus ending the transitional period and restoring de facto independence.</span> </li>

                 <div>
                  <div class="plainlist">
                   <ul>
                    <li><sup>1</sup> <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">Oceanic islands</a> within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.</li>
